      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity">Biodiversity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bahrain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Biodiversity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Birds_in_Al-Areen_Wildlife_Park.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Birds_in_Al-Areen_Wildlife_Park.jpg/220px-Birds_in_Al-Areen_Wildlife_Park.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="330" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Birds_in_Al-Areen_Wildlife_Park.jpg/330px-Birds_in_Al-Areen_Wildlife_Park.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Birds_in_Al-Areen_Wildlife_Park.jpg/440px-Birds_in_Al-Areen_Wildlife_Park.jpg 2x" data-file-width="683" data-file-height="1024"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Birds_in_Al-Areen_Wildlife_Park.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Greater_flamingo" title="Greater flamingo">Greater flamingos</a> (<i>Phoenicopterus roseus</i>) are native to Bahrain.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Bahrain" title="Wildlife of Bahrain">Wildlife of Bahrain</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_birds_of_Bahrain" title="List of birds of Bahrain">List of birds of Bahrain</a>
      </div> 
      <p>More than 330 species of birds were recorded in the Bahrain archipelago, 26 species of which breed in the country. Millions of migratory birds pass through the Persian Gulf region in the winter and autumn months.<sup id="cite_ref-Fuller_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fuller-141">[141]</a></sup> One globally endangered species, <i><a href="/wiki/Houbara_bustard" title="Houbara bustard">Chlamydotis undulata</a></i>, is a regular migrant in the autumn.<sup id="cite_ref-Fuller_141-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fuller-141">[141]</a></sup> The many islands and shallow seas of Bahrain are globally important for the breeding of the <a href="/wiki/Socotra_cormorant" title="Socotra cormorant">Socotra cormorant</a>; up to 100,000 pairs of these birds were recorded over the Hawar islands.<sup id="cite_ref-Fuller_141-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fuller-141">[141]</a></sup> Bahrain's national bird is the <a href="/wiki/Bulbul" title="Bulbul">bulbul</a> while its national animal is the <a href="/wiki/Arabian_oryx" title="Arabian oryx">Arabian oryx</a>. And the national flower of Bahrain is the beloved Deena. </p>
      <p>Only 18 species of mammals are found in Bahrain, animals such as <a href="/wiki/Gazelle" title="Gazelle">gazelles</a>, desert rabbits and <a href="/wiki/Hedgehog" title="Hedgehog">hedgehogs</a> are common in the wild but the <a href="/wiki/Arabian_oryx" title="Arabian oryx">Arabian oryx</a> was hunted to <a href="/wiki/Extinction" title="Extinction">extinction</a> on the island.<sup id="cite_ref-Fuller_141-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fuller-141">[141]</a></sup> Twenty-five species of <a href="/wiki/Amphibian" title="Amphibian">amphibians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Reptile" title="Reptile">reptiles</a> were recorded as well as 21 species of <a href="/wiki/Butterfly" title="Butterfly">butterflies</a> and 307 species of <a href="/wiki/Flora" title="Flora">flora</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Fuller_141-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fuller-141">[141]</a></sup> The marine <a href="/wiki/Biotope" title="Biotope">biotopes</a> are diverse and include extensive <a href="/wiki/Sea_grass" class="mw-redirect" title="Sea grass">sea grass</a> beds and <a href="/wiki/Mudflats" class="mw-redirect" title="Mudflats">mudflats</a>, patchy <a href="/wiki/Coral_reef" title="Coral reef">coral reefs</a> as well as offshore islands. Sea grass beds are important foraging grounds for some threatened species such as <a href="/wiki/Dugong" title="Dugong">dugongs</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Green_turtle" class="mw-redirect" title="Green turtle">green turtle</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CBD_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CBD-142">[142]</a></sup> In 2003, Bahrain banned the capture of <a href="/wiki/Sirenia" title="Sirenia">sea cows</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sea_turtle" title="Sea turtle">marine turtles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dolphin" title="Dolphin">dolphins</a> within its territorial waters.<sup id="cite_ref-Fuller_141-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fuller-141">[141]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Hawar Islands Protected Area provides valuable feeding and breeding grounds for a variety of migratory seabirds, it is an internationally recognised site for <a href="/wiki/Bird_migration" title="Bird migration">bird migration</a>. The breeding colony of <a href="/wiki/Socotra_cormorant" title="Socotra cormorant">Socotra cormorant</a> on Hawar Islands is the largest in the world, and the dugongs foraging around the archipelago form the second-largest dugong aggregation after Australia.<sup id="cite_ref-CBD_142-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CBD-142">[142]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Bahrain has five designated <a href="/wiki/Protected_area" title="Protected area">protected areas</a>, four of which are marine environments.<sup id="cite_ref-Fuller_141-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fuller-141">[141]</a></sup> They are: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Hawar_Islands" title="Hawar Islands">Hawar Islands</a></li> 
       <li>Mashtan Island, off the coast of Bahrain.</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Arad,_Bahrain" title="Arad, Bahrain">Arad</a> bay, in Muharraq.</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Tubli_Bay" title="Tubli Bay">Tubli Bay</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Al_Areen_Wildlife_Park" title="Al Areen Wildlife Park">Al Areen Wildlife Park</a>, which is a zoo and a breeding centre for <a href="/wiki/Endangered_species" title="Endangered species">endangered animals</a>, is the only protected area on land and also the only protected area which is managed on a day-to-day basis.<sup id="cite_ref-Fuller_141-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fuller-141">[141]</a></sup></li>
      </ul> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bahrain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Government and politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Bahrain" title="Politics of Bahrain">Politics of Bahrain</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Hamad-Bin-Isa-Al-Khalifa.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Hamad-Bin-Isa-Al-Khalifa.jpg/220px-Hamad-Bin-Isa-Al-Khalifa.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="336" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Hamad-Bin-Isa-Al-Khalifa.jpg/330px-Hamad-Bin-Isa-Al-Khalifa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Hamad-Bin-Isa-Al-Khalifa.jpg/440px-Hamad-Bin-Isa-Al-Khalifa.jpg 2x" data-file-width="897" data-file-height="1371"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Hamad-Bin-Isa-Al-Khalifa.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Shaikh Hamad bin Isa Al Khalifa, the King of Bahrain
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Bahrain under the Al-Khalifa is a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a> headed by the <a href="/wiki/King_of_Bahrain" title="King of Bahrain">King</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hamad_bin_Isa_Al_Khalifa" title="Hamad bin Isa Al Khalifa">Shaikh Hamad bin Isa Al Khalifa</a>. King Hamad enjoys wide executive powers which include appointing the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Bahrain" title="Prime Minister of Bahrain">Prime Minister</a> and his <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_Bahrain" title="Cabinet of Bahrain">ministers</a>, commanding the <a href="/wiki/Bahrain_Defence_Force" title="Bahrain Defence Force">army</a>, chairing the <a href="/wiki/Judiciary_of_Bahrain" title="Judiciary of Bahrain">Higher Judicial Council</a>, appointing the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_(Bahrain)" title="National Assembly (Bahrain)">parliament</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Consultative_Council_(Bahrain)" title="Consultative Council (Bahrain)">upper house</a> and dissolving its elected <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Representatives_(Bahrain)" title="Council of Representatives (Bahrain)">lower house</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-143">[143]</a></sup> The head of government is the prime minister. In 2010, about half of the <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_Bahrain" title="Cabinet of Bahrain">government</a> was composed of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Khalifa" title="House of Khalifa">Al Khalifa family</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Bahrain has a <a href="/wiki/Bicameralism" title="Bicameralism">bicameral</a> National Assembly (<i>al-Jam'iyyah al-Watani</i>) consisting of the Shura Council (<i>Majlis Al-Shura</i>) with 40 seats and the Council of Representatives (<i>Majlis Al-Nuwab</i>) with 40 seats. The forty members of the Shura are appointed by the king. In the Council of Representatives, 40 members are elected by absolute majority vote in single-member constituencies to serve four-year terms.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> The appointed council "exercises a <i>de facto</i> veto" over the elected, because draft acts must be approved so they may pass into law. After approval, the king may ratify and issue the act or return it within six months to the National Assembly where it may only pass into law if approved by two thirds of both councils.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_143-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-143">[143]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1973, the country held its first <a href="/wiki/Bahraini_general_election,_1973" class="mw-redirect" title="Bahraini general election, 1973">parliamentary elections</a>; however, two years later, the <a href="/wiki/Isa_bin_Salman_Al_Khalifa" title="Isa bin Salman Al Khalifa">late emir</a> dissolved the parliament and suspended the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Bahrain#Constitution_of_1973" title="Constitution of Bahrain">constitution</a> after parliament rejected the <a href="/wiki/State_Security_Law_in_Bahrain" title="State Security Law in Bahrain">State Security Law</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_11.5.2012_97-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_11.5.2012-97">[97]</a></sup> The period between 2002 and 2010 saw three parliamentary elections. The <a href="/wiki/Bahraini_parliamentary_election,_2002" class="mw-redirect" title="Bahraini parliamentary election, 2002">first</a>, held in 2002 was boycotted by the opposition, <a href="/wiki/Al_Wefaq" title="Al Wefaq">Al Wefaq</a>, which won a majority in the <a href="/wiki/Bahraini_general_election,_2006" class="mw-redirect" title="Bahraini general election, 2006">second</a> in 2006 and <a href="/wiki/Bahraini_general_election,_2010" class="mw-redirect" title="Bahraini general election, 2010">third</a> in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Bahraini_parliamentary_by-election,_2011" class="mw-redirect" title="Bahraini parliamentary by-election, 2011">2011 by-election</a> was held to replace 18 members of Al Wefaq who resigned in protest against government crackdown.<sup id="cite_ref-ThReut_boycott_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ThReut_boycott-147">[147]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYT_violence_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT_violence-148">[148]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The opening up of politics saw big gains for both <a href="/wiki/Shia_Islam" title="Shia Islam">Shīa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sunn%C4%AB" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunnī">Sunnī</a> <a href="/wiki/Islamists" class="mw-redirect" title="Islamists">Islamists</a> in elections, which gave them a parliamentary platform to pursue their policies.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> It gave a new prominence to clerics within the political system, with the most senior Shia religious leader, Sheikh <a href="/wiki/Isa_Qassim" title="Isa Qassim">Isa Qassim</a>, playing a vital role.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> This was especially evident when in 2005 the government called off the Shia branch of the "Family law" after over 100,000 Shia took to the streets. Islamists opposed the law because "neither elected MPs nor the government has the authority to change the law because these institutions could misinterpret the word of God". The law was supported by women activists who said they were "suffering in silence". They managed to organise a rally attended by 500 participants.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ghada_Jamsheer" class="mw-redirect" title="Ghada Jamsheer">Ghada Jamsheer</a>, a leading woman activist<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> said the government was using the law as a "bargaining tool with opposition Islamic groups".<sup id="cite_ref-GJ_18.12.2006_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GJ_18.12.2006-155">[155]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Analysts of democratisation in the Middle East cite the Islamists' references to respect human rights in their justification for these programmes as evidence that these groups can serve as a progressive force in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> Some Islamist parties have been particularly critical of the government's readiness to sign international treaties such as the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>' International Convention on Civil and Political Rights. At a parliamentary session in June 2006 to discuss ratification of the Convention, Sheikh <a href="/wiki/Adel_Mouwda" title="Adel Mouwda">Adel Mouwda</a>, the former leader of <a href="/wiki/Salafi_movement" title="Salafi movement">salafist</a> party, <a href="/wiki/Al_Asalah" title="Al Asalah">Asalah</a>, explained the party's objections: "The convention has been tailored by our enemies, God kill them all, to serve their needs and protect their interests rather than ours. This why we have eyes from the American Embassy watching us during our sessions, to ensure things are swinging their way".<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bahrain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bahrain_Defence_Force" title="Bahrain Defence Force">Bahrain Defence Force</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Peninsula_Shield_Force" title="Peninsula Shield Force">Peninsula Shield Force</a> and <a href="/wiki/Naval_Support_Activity_Bahrain" title="Naval Support Activity Bahrain">Naval Support Activity Bahrain</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:RBNS_Sabha_(FFG_90)_Bahrain.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/RBNS_Sabha_%28FFG_90%29_Bahrain.jpg/220px-RBNS_Sabha_%28FFG_90%29_Bahrain.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/RBNS_Sabha_%28FFG_90%29_Bahrain.jpg/330px-RBNS_Sabha_%28FFG_90%29_Bahrain.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/RBNS_Sabha_%28FFG_90%29_Bahrain.jpg/440px-RBNS_Sabha_%28FFG_90%29_Bahrain.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2100" data-file-height="1500"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:RBNS_Sabha_(FFG_90)_Bahrain.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/RBNS_Sabha_(FFG-90)" title="RBNS Sabha (FFG-90)">RBNS&nbsp;<i>Sabha</i></a> of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Bahraini_Navy" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Bahraini Navy">Royal Bahraini Navy</a> taking part in a multilateral sea exercise
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The kingdom has a small but well equipped military called the Bahrain Defence Force (BDF), numbering around 13,000 personnel.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup> The supreme commander of the Bahraini military is King <a href="/wiki/Hamad_bin_Isa_Al_Khalifa" title="Hamad bin Isa Al Khalifa">Hamad bin Isa Al Khalifa</a> and the deputy supreme commander is the Crown Prince, <a href="/wiki/Salman_bin_Hamad_bin_Isa_Al_Khalifa" class="mw-redirect" title="Salman bin Hamad bin Isa Al Khalifa">Salman bin Hamad bin Isa Al Khalifa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The BDF is primarily equipped with United States equipment, such as the <a href="/wiki/F-16_Fighting_Falcon" class="mw-redirect" title="F-16 Fighting Falcon">F-16 Fighting Falcon</a>, <a href="/wiki/F-5_Freedom_Fighter" class="mw-redirect" title="F-5 Freedom Fighter">F-5 Freedom Fighter</a>, <a href="/wiki/UH-60_Blackhawk" class="mw-redirect" title="UH-60 Blackhawk">UH-60 Blackhawk</a>, <a href="/wiki/M60_Patton" class="mw-redirect" title="M60 Patton">M60A3 tanks</a>, and the ex-<a href="/wiki/USS_Jack_Williams_(FFG-24)" title="USS Jack Williams (FFG-24)">USS&nbsp;<i>Jack Williams</i></a>, an <a href="/wiki/Oliver_Hazard_Perry_class_frigate" class="mw-redirect" title="Oliver Hazard Perry class frigate">Oliver Hazard Perry class frigate</a> renamed the <a href="/wiki/RBNS_Sabha_(FFG-90)" title="RBNS Sabha (FFG-90)">RBNS&nbsp;<i>Sabha</i></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup> On 7 August 2020, it was announced in a ceremony held at the <a href="/wiki/HMNB_Portsmouth" title="HMNB Portsmouth">HMNB Portsmouth Naval Base</a> in the <a href="/wiki/UK" class="mw-redirect" title="UK">UK</a>, that <i><a href="/wiki/HMS_Clyde_(P257)" title="HMS Clyde (P257)">HMS Clyde</a></i> had been transferred to the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Bahrain_Naval_Force" title="Royal Bahrain Naval Force">Royal Bahrain Naval Force</a>, with the ship renamed as <a href="/wiki/Royal_Bahrain_Naval_Force#Fleet" title="Royal Bahrain Naval Force">RBNS <i>Al-Zubara</i></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Government of Bahrain has <a href="/wiki/Bahrain%E2%80%93United_States_relations" title="Bahrain–United States relations">close relations</a> with the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, having signed a cooperative agreement with the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Armed_Forces" title="United States Armed Forces">United States Military</a> and has provided the United States a base in <a href="/wiki/Juffair" title="Juffair">Juffair</a> since the early 1990s, although a US naval presence existed since 1948.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup> This is the home of the headquarters for Commander, <i>United States Naval Forces Central Command</i> (<a href="/wiki/COMUSNAVCENT" class="mw-redirect" title="COMUSNAVCENT">COMUSNAVCENT</a>) / <i>United States Fifth Fleet</i> (COMFIFTHFLT),<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> and around 6,000 United States military personnel.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Bahrain participates in the <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabian-led_intervention_in_Yemen" title="Saudi Arabian-led intervention in Yemen">Saudi Arabian-led intervention in Yemen</a> against the <a href="/wiki/Shia_Islam" title="Shia Islam">Shia</a> <a href="/wiki/Houthis" class="mw-redirect" title="Houthis">Houthis</a> and forces loyal to former President <a href="/wiki/Ali_Abdullah_Saleh" title="Ali Abdullah Saleh">Ali Abdullah Saleh</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup> who was deposed in the 2011 <a href="/wiki/Arab_Spring" title="Arab Spring">Arab Spring</a> uprising.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The permanent British <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a> base at <a href="/wiki/Mina_Salman" title="Mina Salman">Mina Salman</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/HMS_Jufair" title="HMS Jufair">HMS Jufair</a></i>, was officially opened in April 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bahrain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Bahrain" title="Foreign relations of Bahrain">Foreign relations of Bahrain</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Donald_Trump_meets_with_King_Hamed_bin_Issa_of_Bahrain,_May_2017.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Donald_Trump_meets_with_King_Hamed_bin_Issa_of_Bahrain%2C_May_2017.jpg/220px-Donald_Trump_meets_with_King_Hamed_bin_Issa_of_Bahrain%2C_May_2017.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Donald_Trump_meets_with_King_Hamed_bin_Issa_of_Bahrain%2C_May_2017.jpg/330px-Donald_Trump_meets_with_King_Hamed_bin_Issa_of_Bahrain%2C_May_2017.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Donald_Trump_meets_with_King_Hamed_bin_Issa_of_Bahrain%2C_May_2017.jpg/440px-Donald_Trump_meets_with_King_Hamed_bin_Issa_of_Bahrain%2C_May_2017.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="800"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">

         </div>King <a href="/wiki/Hamad_bin_Isa_Al_Khalifa" title="Hamad bin Isa Al Khalifa">Hamad bin Isa Al Khalifa</a> meets U.S. President <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a>, May 2017
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:US_Navy_061105-N-3455P-002_USS_Boxer_(LHD_4)_and_ships_assigned_to_Boxer_Expeditionary_Strike_Group_(BOXESG)_steam_alongside_while_transiting_to_U.S._5th_Fleet%27s_area_of_responsibility.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/US_Navy_061105-N-3455P-002_USS_Boxer_%28LHD_4%29_and_ships_assigned_to_Boxer_Expeditionary_Strike_Group_%28BOXESG%29_steam_alongside_while_transiting_to_U.S._5th_Fleet%27s_area_of_responsibility.jpg/220px-thumbnail.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/US_Navy_061105-N-3455P-002_USS_Boxer_%28LHD_4%29_and_ships_assigned_to_Boxer_Expeditionary_Strike_Group_%28BOXESG%29_steam_alongside_while_transiting_to_U.S._5th_Fleet%27s_area_of_responsibility.jpg/330px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/US_Navy_061105-N-3455P-002_USS_Boxer_%28LHD_4%29_and_ships_assigned_to_Boxer_Expeditionary_Strike_Group_%28BOXESG%29_steam_alongside_while_transiting_to_U.S._5th_Fleet%27s_area_of_responsibility.jpg/440px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2944" data-file-height="1888"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:US_Navy_061105-N-3455P-002_USS_Boxer_(LHD_4)_and_ships_assigned_to_Boxer_Expeditionary_Strike_Group_(BOXESG)_steam_alongside_while_transiting_to_U.S._5th_Fleet%27s_area_of_responsibility.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Bahrain is the headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Navy" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Navy">U.S. Navy</a>'s <a href="/wiki/United_States_Fifth_Fleet" title="United States Fifth Fleet">Fifth Fleet</a> responsible for naval forces in the <a href="/wiki/Persian_Gulf" title="Persian Gulf">Persian Gulf</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Bahrain has established <a href="/wiki/Bilateral_relations" class="mw-redirect" title="Bilateral relations">bilateral relations</a> with 190 countries worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup> As of 2012<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bahrain&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Bahrain maintains a network of 25 <a href="/wiki/Embassies" class="mw-redirect" title="Embassies">embassies</a>, 3 <a href="/wiki/Consulates" class="mw-redirect" title="Consulates">consulates</a> and 4 permanent missions to the Arab League, United Nations and <a href="/wiki/Bahrain%E2%80%93European_Union_relations" title="Bahrain–European Union relations">European Union</a> respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup> Bahrain also hosts 36 embassies. Bahrain plays a modest, moderating role in regional politics and adheres to the views of the Arab League on Middle East peace and <a href="/wiki/State_of_Palestine" title="State of Palestine">Palestinian</a> rights by supporting the <a href="/wiki/Two_state_solution" class="mw-redirect" title="Two state solution">two state solution</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup> Bahrain is also one of the founding members of the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Cooperation_Council" title="Gulf Cooperation Council">Gulf Cooperation Council</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup> Relations with Iran tend to be tense as a result of a <a href="/wiki/1981_Bahraini_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat_attempt" title="1981 Bahraini coup d'état attempt">failed coup</a> in 1981 which Bahrain blames Iran for and occasional claims of Iranian sovereignty over Bahrain by <a href="/wiki/Conservatism" title="Conservatism">ultra-conservative</a> elements in the Iranian public.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabian_Army" title="Saudi Arabian Army">Saudi Arabian troops</a> were sent into Bahrain to crush pro-democracy protests in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Bahrain first welcomed Israeli cabinet member <a href="/wiki/Yossi_Sarid" title="Yossi Sarid">Yossi Sarid</a> to Manama in 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup> In September 2020, after the <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a> announced normalizing relations with <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>, Bahrain announced that it would allow all commercial flights coming from Israel to fly over its airspace<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup> On 11 September 2020, U.S. President <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a> announced that Bahrain and <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a> were to normalize relations under the <a href="/wiki/Bahrain%E2%80%93Israel_peace_agreement" class="mw-redirect" title="Bahrain–Israel peace agreement">Bahrain–Israel peace agreement</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup> Bahrain's official recognition of the State of Israel followed its GCC neighbor Oman's hosting of the Israeli prime minister in 2018<sup id="cite_ref-jpost.com_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jpost.com-181">[181]</a></sup> as well as the UAE's official recognition of the State of Israel in August 2020. Bahrain's decision was very likely approved in advance by the Kingdom of <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-jpost.com_181-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jpost.com-181">[181]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bahrain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Human rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The period between 1975 and 1999 known as the "<a href="/wiki/State_Security_Law_in_Bahrain" title="State Security Law in Bahrain">State Security Law Era</a>", saw wide range of human rights violations including arbitrary arrests, detention without trial, torture and forced exile.<sup id="cite_ref-Amnesty_27.9.1995_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Amnesty_27.9.1995-182">[182]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-HRW_1.6.1997_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HRW_1.6.1997-183">[183]</a></sup> After the Emir Hamad Al Khalifa (now king) succeeded his father Isa Al Khalifa in 1999, he introduced wide reforms and human rights improved significantly.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup> These moves were described by <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a> as representing a "historic period of human rights".<sup id="cite_ref-AI_Bahr_promising_107-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AI_Bahr_promising-107">[107]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Human rights conditions started to decline by 2007 when <a href="/wiki/Torture_in_Bahrain" title="Torture in Bahrain">torture</a> began to be employed again.<sup id="cite_ref-HRW_Torture_Redux_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HRW_Torture_Redux-185">[185]</a></sup> In 2011, <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a> described the country's human rights situation as "dismal".<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup> Due to this, Bahrain lost some of the high <a href="/wiki/International_rankings_of_Bahrain" title="International rankings of Bahrain">International rankings</a> it had gained before.<sup id="cite_ref-Freedom_in_the_World_2012_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Freedom_in_the_World_2012-187">[187]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FH_FotN_2011_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FH_FotN_2011-188">[188]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RWB_2002_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RWB_2002-189">[189]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RWB_2010_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RWB_2010-190">[190]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FH_Press_Freedom_2011_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FH_Press_Freedom_2011-191">[191]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2011, Bahrain was criticised for its crackdown on the <a href="/wiki/Bahraini_uprising_of_2011" title="Bahraini uprising of 2011">Arab spring uprising</a>. In September, a government-appointed <a href="/wiki/Bahrain_Independent_Commission_of_Inquiry" title="Bahrain Independent Commission of Inquiry">commission</a> confirmed <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_reports_on_the_Bahraini_uprising_of_2011" title="Human rights reports on the Bahraini uprising of 2011">reports</a> of grave human rights violations, including <a href="/wiki/Torture_during_the_Bahraini_uprising_(2011%E2%80%93present)" title="Torture during the Bahraini uprising (2011–present)">systematic torture</a>. The government promised to introduce reforms and avoid repeating the "painful events".<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup> However, reports by human rights organisations Amnesty International and Human Rights Watch issued in April 2012 said the same violations were still happening.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The documentary TV film <i><a href="/wiki/Bahrain:_Shouting_in_the_Dark" title="Bahrain: Shouting in the Dark">Bahrain: Shouting in the Dark</a></i>, which was produced by the Qatari channel <a href="/wiki/Al_Jazeera" title="Al Jazeera">Al Jazeera</a>, talks about the Bahraini protests during 2011. This TV film showed all the violations that have been taken against the rights of Bahraini citizens during the uprising. It also caused some problems between the Bahraini and the Qatari governments.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AJStream_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AJStream-196">[196]</a></sup> Relations between Bahrain and Qatar improved following a meeting of the Gulf Cooperation Council in November 2014 in which it was announced Bahrain diplomats would return to Qatar.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a>'s 2015 report on the country points to continued suppression of dissent, restricted freedom of expression, unjust imprisonment, and frequent torture and other ill-treatment of its citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a> in its 2015 report described the situation of a Shia majority as more than tragic.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Freedom_House" title="Freedom House">Freedom House</a> labels Bahrain as "not free" in its 2016 report.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup> On 7 July 2016, the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a> adopted, with a large majority, a resolution condemning human rights abuses performed by Bahraini authorities, and strongly called for an end to the ongoing repression against the country's human rights defenders, political opposition and civil society.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Sit-in_in_solidarity_with_Nabeel_Rajab.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Sit-in_in_solidarity_with_Nabeel_Rajab.JPG/220px-Sit-in_in_solidarity_with_Nabeel_Rajab.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Sit-in_in_solidarity_with_Nabeel_Rajab.JPG/330px-Sit-in_in_solidarity_with_Nabeel_Rajab.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Sit-in_in_solidarity_with_Nabeel_Rajab.JPG/440px-Sit-in_in_solidarity_with_Nabeel_Rajab.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Sit-in_in_solidarity_with_Nabeel_Rajab.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A number of people held a sit-in in solidarity with human rights activist <a href="/wiki/Nabeel_Rajab" title="Nabeel Rajab">Nabeel Rajab</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In August 2017, United States Secretary of State <a href="/wiki/Rex_Tillerson" title="Rex Tillerson">Rex Tillerson</a> spoke against the discrimination of Shias in Bahrain, saying, "Members of the Shia community there continue to report ongoing discrimination in government employment, education, and the justice system," and that "Bahrain must stop discriminating against the Shia communities." He also stated that "In Bahrain, the government continue to question, detain and arrest Shia clerics, community members and opposition politicians."<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup> However, in September 2017, the U.S. State Department has approved arms sales packages worth more than $3.8 billion to Bahrain including F-16 jets, upgrades, missiles and patrol boats.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">[205]</a></sup> In its latest report the <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a> accused both, US and the UK governments, of turning a blind eye to horrific abuses of human rights by the ruling Bahraini regime.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">[206]</a></sup> On 31 January 2018, Amnesty International reported that the Bahraini government expelled four of its citizens after having revoked their nationality in 2012; turning them into stateless people.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup> On 21 February 2018, human rights activist <a href="/wiki/Nabeel_Rajab" title="Nabeel Rajab">Nabeel Rajab</a> was sentenced to a further five years in jail for tweets and documentation of human rights violations.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">[208]</a></sup> On behalf of the ruling family, Bahraini police have received training on how to deal with public protests from the British government.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Reliable sources"><span title="The material near this tag may rely on an unreliable source. (December 2018)">unreliable source?</span></a></i>]</sup><sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">[210]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 11 July 2020, a government watchdog in Bahrain claimed that the confessions of two pro-democracy campaigners were extracted by torture. Mohammed Ramadhan and Husain Moosa from Bahrain were leading figures in the pro-democracy protests of 2011. They were arrested in 2014 and accused of killing a police officer.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup> On July 13, 2020, the highest Court in Bahrain overruled the previous judgment and upheld the death sentences for both men. The judgment was criticized by Sayed Ahmed Alwadaei, the director of advocacy at the <a href="/wiki/Bahrain_Institute_for_Rights_and_Democracy" title="Bahrain Institute for Rights and Democracy">Bahrain Institute for Rights and Democracy</a>, who stated: “Today’s verdict is yet another dark stain in the struggle for human rights in Bahrain.”<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The 761-page <i>World Report 2021</i> published by the <i><a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a></i> in January 2021 revealed that the situation of human rights didn’t improve in Bahrain in 2020. It highlighted that the repression against social media activities escalated, death sentences were upheld by the courts against opposition activists after unfair trials, and the critics were continued to be prosecuted for peaceful expression. The country also increased the use of the death penalty, while it denied medical treatment to some of the prominent opposition figures being kept in detention. The <i>Human Rights Watch</i> said that Bahrain uses several repressive tools to silence and punish every person who dares to criticize the government.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="Women.27s_rights"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Women's_rights">Women's rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bahrain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Women's rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_rights_in_Bahrain" title="Women's rights in Bahrain">Women's rights in Bahrain</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Women in Bahrain acquired voting rights and the right to stand in national elections in the 2002 election.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup> However, no women were elected to office in that year's polls.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">[215]</a></sup> In response to the failure of women candidates, six were appointed to the Shura Council, which also includes representatives of the Kingdom's indigenous Jewish and Christian communities.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup> Dr. <a href="/wiki/Nada_Haffadh" title="Nada Haffadh">Nada Haffadh</a> became the country's first female cabinet minister on her appointment as Minister of Health in 2004. The quasi-governmental women's group, the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Council_for_Women" title="Supreme Council for Women">Supreme Council for Women</a>, trained female candidates to take part in the 2006 general election. When Bahrain was elected to head the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">United Nations General Assembly</a> in 2006 it appointed lawyer and women's rights activist <a href="/wiki/Haya_Rashed_Al-Khalifa" title="Haya Rashed Al-Khalifa">Haya bint Rashid Al Khalifa</a> President of the United Nations General Assembly, only the third woman in history to head the world body.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">[217]</a></sup> Female activist Ghada Jamsheer said "The government used women's rights as a decorative tool on the international level." She referred to the reforms as "artificial and marginal" and accused the government of "hinder[ing] non-governmental women societies".<sup id="cite_ref-GJ_18.12.2006_155-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GJ_18.12.2006-155">[155]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2006, <a href="/wiki/Lateefa_Al_Gaood" title="Lateefa Al Gaood">Lateefa Al Gaood</a> became the first female MP after winning by default.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">[218]</a></sup> The number rose to four after the 2011 by-elections.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">[219]</a></sup> In 2008, <a href="/wiki/Houda_Nonoo" title="Houda Nonoo">Houda Nonoo</a> was appointed ambassador to the United States making her the first Jewish ambassador of any Arab country.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">[220]</a></sup> In 2011, <a href="/wiki/Alees_Samaan" title="Alees Samaan">Alice Samaan</a>, a Christian woman, was appointed ambassador to the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">[221]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bahrain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The predominant forms of media in Bahrain consists of weekly and daily newspapers, television, and radio. </p>
      <p>Newspapers are widely available in multiple languages such as Arabic, English, Malayalam, etc. to support the varied population. <i><a href="/wiki/Akhbar_Al_Khaleej" title="Akhbar Al Khaleej">Akhbar Al Khaleej</a></i> (أخبار الخليج) and <i><a href="/wiki/Al_Ayam_(Bahrain)" title="Al Ayam (Bahrain)">Al Ayam</a></i> (الأيام) are examples of major Arabic newspapers published daily. <i><a href="/wiki/Gulf_Daily_News" title="Gulf Daily News">Gulf Daily News</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_Tribune_(Bahrain)" title="Daily Tribune (Bahrain)">Daily Tribune</a></i> publish daily newspapers in English. <i><a href="/wiki/Gulf_Madhyamam" class="mw-redirect" title="Gulf Madhyamam">Gulf Madhyamam</a></i> is a newspaper published in Malayalam. </p>
      <p>The country's television network operates over 5 networks, all of which are by the <a href="/wiki/Information_Affairs_Authority" title="Information Affairs Authority">Information Affairs Authority</a>. Radio, much like the television network, is mostly state-run and usually in Arabic. <i>Radio Bahrain</i> is a long-running English language radio station and <i>Your FM</i> is a radio station serving the large expatriate population from the Indian Subcontinent living in the country. </p>
      <p>By June 2012, Bahrain had 961,000 internet users.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_222-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-222">[222]</a></sup> The platform "provides a welcome free space for journalists, although one that is increasingly monitored", according to <a href="/wiki/Reporters_Without_Borders" title="Reporters Without Borders">Reporters Without Borders</a>. Rigorous filtering targets political, human rights, religious material and content deemed obscene. Bloggers and other <a href="/wiki/Netizens" class="mw-redirect" title="Netizens">netizens</a> were among those detained during protests in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_223-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-223">[223]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Bahraini journalists risk prosecution for offenses which include "undermining" the government and religion. <a href="/wiki/Self-censorship" title="Self-censorship">Self-censorship</a> is widespread. Journalists were targeted by officials during anti-government protests in 2011. Three editors from opposition daily <a href="/wiki/Al-Wasat_(Bahraini_newspaper)" title="Al-Wasat (Bahraini newspaper)"><i>Al-Wasat</i></a> were sacked and later fined for publishing "false" news. Several foreign correspondents were expelled.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_223-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-223">[223]</a></sup> An independent commission, set up to look into the unrest, found that state media coverage was at times inflammatory. It said opposition groups suffered from lack of access to mainstream media, and recommended that the government "consider relaxing censorship". Bahrain will host the Saudi-financed <a href="/wiki/Alarab_News_Channel" class="mw-redirect" title="Alarab News Channel">Alarab News Channel</a>, expected to launch in December 2012. It will be based at a planned "Media City". An opposition satellite station, <a href="/wiki/LuaLua_TV" title="LuaLua TV">LuaLua TV</a>, operates from London but has found its signals blocked.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_223-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-223">[223]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Governorates">Governorates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bahrain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Governorates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Governorates_of_Bahrain" title="Governorates of Bahrain">Governorates of Bahrain</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The first <a href="/wiki/Municipality" title="Municipality">municipality</a> in Bahrain was the 8-member <a href="/wiki/Manama" title="Manama">Manama</a> municipality which was established in July 1919.<sup id="cite_ref-MMAUP_224-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MMAUP-224">[224]</a></sup> Members of the municipality were elected annually; the municipality was said to have been the first municipality to be established in the <a href="/wiki/Arab_world" title="Arab world">Arab world</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-MMAUP_224-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MMAUP-224">[224]</a></sup> The municipality was in charge of cleaning roads and renting buildings to tenants and shops. By 1929, it undertook road expansions as well as opening markets and <a href="/wiki/Slaughterhouse" title="Slaughterhouse">slaughterhouses</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-MMAUP_224-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MMAUP-224">[224]</a></sup> In 1958, the municipality started <a href="/wiki/Water_purification" title="Water purification">water purification</a> projects.<sup id="cite_ref-MMAUP_224-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MMAUP-224">[224]</a></sup> In 1960, Bahrain comprised four municipalities: <i>Manama</i>, <i>Hidd</i>, <i>Al Muharraq</i>, and <i>Riffa</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Statoids_225-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Statoids-225">[225]</a></sup> Over the next 30 years, the 4 municipalities were divided into 12 municipalities as settlements such as <a href="/wiki/Hamad_Town" title="Hamad Town">Hamad Town</a> and <a href="/wiki/Isa_Town" title="Isa Town">Isa Town</a> grew.<sup id="cite_ref-Statoids_225-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Statoids-225">[225]</a></sup> These municipalities were administered from <a href="/wiki/Manama" title="Manama">Manama</a> under a central municipal council whose members are appointed by the king.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">[226]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The first municipal elections to be held in Bahrain after independence in 1971, was in 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">[227]</a></sup> The most recent was in 2010. The municipalities are listed below: </p>

      <p>After 3 July 2002, Bahrain was split into five administrative <a href="/wiki/Governorates" class="mw-redirect" title="Governorates">governorates</a>, each of which has its own <a href="/wiki/Governor" title="Governor">governor</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">[228]</a></sup> These governorates are: </p> 
      <table class="wikitable"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th>Map</th> 
         <th>Former Governorates </th>

         <td rowspan="5"><a href="/wiki/File:Governorates_of_Bahrain.svg" class="image"><img alt="Governorates of Bahrain.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Governorates_of_Bahrain.svg/256px-Governorates_of_Bahrain.svg.png" decoding="async" width="256" height="379" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Governorates_of_Bahrain.svg/384px-Governorates_of_Bahrain.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Governorates_of_Bahrain.svg/512px-Governorates_of_Bahrain.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="677" data-file-height="1003"></a></td>
