      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bahrain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Bahrain" title="Education in Bahrain">Education in Bahrain</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_universities_in_Bahrain" title="List of universities in Bahrain">List of universities in Bahrain</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:University_students_Bahrain.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/University_students_Bahrain.jpg/220px-University_students_Bahrain.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/University_students_Bahrain.jpg/330px-University_students_Bahrain.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/University_students_Bahrain.jpg/440px-University_students_Bahrain.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="535"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:University_students_Bahrain.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Female students at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Bahrain" title="University of Bahrain">University of Bahrain</a> dressed in traditional garb
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Education is compulsory for children between the ages of 6 and 14.<sup id="cite_ref-291" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-291">[291]</a></sup> Education is free for Bahraini citizens in <a href="/wiki/State_school" title="State school">public schools</a>, with the Bahraini <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Education_(Bahrain)" title="Ministry of Education (Bahrain)">Ministry of Education</a> providing free textbooks. <a href="/wiki/Coeducation" class="mw-redirect" title="Coeducation">Coeducation</a> is not used in public schools, with boys and girls segregated into separate schools.<sup id="cite_ref-292" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-292">[292]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>At the beginning of the 20th century, Qur'anic schools (<i><a href="/wiki/Kuttab" title="Kuttab">Kuttab</a></i>) were the only form of education in Bahrain.<sup id="cite_ref-MoE_293-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MoE-293">[293]</a></sup> They were traditional schools aimed at teaching children and youth the reading of the <a href="/wiki/Qur%27an" class="mw-redirect" title="Qur'an">Qur'an</a>. After <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, Bahrain became open to western influences, and a demand for modern educational institutions appeared. 1919 marked the beginning of modern public school system in Bahrain when the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Al-Hidaya_Al-Khalifia_School&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Al-Hidaya Al-Khalifia School (page does not exist)">Al-Hidaya Al-Khalifia School</a> for boys opened in <a href="/wiki/Muharraq" title="Muharraq">Muharraq</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-MoE_293-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MoE-293">[293]</a></sup> In 1926, the Education Committee opened the second public school for boys in <a href="/wiki/Manama" title="Manama">Manama</a>, and in 1928 the first public school for girls was opened in Muharraq.<sup id="cite_ref-MoE_293-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MoE-293">[293]</a></sup> As of 2011<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Bahrain&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, there are a total of 126,981 students studying in public schools.<sup id="cite_ref-294" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-294">[294]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2004, King <a href="/wiki/Hamad_ibn_Isa_Al_Khalifa" class="mw-redirect" title="Hamad ibn Isa Al Khalifa">Hamad ibn Isa Al Khalifa</a> introduced the "King Hamad Schools of Future" project that uses Information Communication Technology to support <a href="/wiki/K%E2%80%9312_education" class="mw-redirect" title="K–12 education">K–12 education</a> in Bahrain.<sup id="cite_ref-295" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-295">[295]</a></sup> The project's objective is to connect all schools within the kingdom with the Internet.<sup id="cite_ref-296" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-296">[296]</a></sup> In addition to British intermediate schools, the island is served by the <a href="/wiki/Bahrain_School" title="Bahrain School">Bahrain School</a> (BS). The BS is a <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Defense" title="United States Department of Defense">United States Department of Defense</a> school that provides a K-12 curriculum including <a href="/wiki/International_Baccalaureate" title="International Baccalaureate">International Baccalaureate</a> offerings. There are also private schools that offer either the <a href="/wiki/IB_Diploma_Programme" title="IB Diploma Programme">IB Diploma Programme</a> or United Kingdom's <a href="/wiki/A-Levels" class="mw-redirect" title="A-Levels">A-Levels</a>. </p>
      <p>Bahrain also encourages institutions of higher learning, drawing on expatriate talent and the increasing pool of Bahrain nationals returning from abroad with advanced degrees. The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Bahrain" title="University of Bahrain">University of Bahrain</a> was established for standard undergraduate and graduate study, and the <a href="/wiki/King_Abdulaziz_University_College_of_Health_Sciences" title="King Abdulaziz University College of Health Sciences">King Abdulaziz University College of Health Sciences</a>, operating under the direction of the Ministry of Health, trains <a href="/wiki/Physician" title="Physician">physicians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nursing" title="Nursing">nurses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pharmacist" title="Pharmacist">pharmacists</a> and <a href="/wiki/Paramedic" title="Paramedic">paramedics</a>. The 2001 National Action Charter paved the way for the formation of private universities such as the <a href="/wiki/Ahlia_University" title="Ahlia University">Ahlia University</a> in Manama and <a href="/wiki/University_College_of_Bahrain" title="University College of Bahrain">University College of Bahrain</a> in <a href="/wiki/Saar,_Bahrain" class="mw-redirect" title="Saar, Bahrain">Saar</a>. The Royal University for Women (RUW), established in 2005, was the first private, purpose-built, international university in Bahrain dedicated solely to educating women. The <a href="/wiki/University_of_London" title="University of London">University of London</a> External has appointed MCG (Management Consultancy Group) as the regional representative office in Bahrain for distance learning programmes.<sup id="cite_ref-297" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-297">[297]</a></sup> MCG is one of the oldest private institutes in the country. Institutes have also opened which educate South Asian students, such as the <a href="/wiki/Pakistan_Urdu_School,_Bahrain" class="mw-redirect" title="Pakistan Urdu School, Bahrain">Pakistan Urdu School, Bahrain</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Indian_School,_Bahrain" title="Indian School, Bahrain">Indian School, Bahrain</a>. A few prominent institutions are the <a href="/wiki/American_University_of_Bahrain" title="American University of Bahrain">American University of Bahrain</a> established in 2019,<sup id="cite_ref-298" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-298">[298]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Bahrain_Institute_of_Banking_and_Finance" title="Bahrain Institute of Banking and Finance">Bahrain Institute of Banking and Finance</a>, the Ernst &amp; Young Training Institute, and the <a href="/wiki/Birla_Institute_of_Technology_International_Centre" title="Birla Institute of Technology International Centre">Birla Institute of Technology International Centre</a>. In 2004, the <a href="/wiki/Royal_College_of_Surgeons_in_Ireland" title="Royal College of Surgeons in Ireland">Royal College of Surgeons in Ireland</a> (RCSI) set up a constituent <a href="/wiki/RCSI-Bahrain" title="RCSI-Bahrain">medical university</a> in the country. In addition to the <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Gulf_University" title="Arabian Gulf University">Arabian Gulf University</a>, <a href="/wiki/AMA_International_University" title="AMA International University">AMA International University</a> and the <a href="/wiki/College_of_Health_Sciences,_Bahrain" class="mw-redirect" title="College of Health Sciences, Bahrain">College of Health Sciences</a>, these are the only medical schools in Bahrain. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bahrain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Bahrain" title="Health in Bahrain">Health in Bahrain</a> and <a href="/wiki/Healthcare_in_Bahrain" title="Healthcare in Bahrain">Healthcare in Bahrain</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:IHB_Ambulance.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/IHB_Ambulance.jpg/220px-IHB_Ambulance.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/IHB_Ambulance.jpg/330px-IHB_Ambulance.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/IHB_Ambulance.jpg/440px-IHB_Ambulance.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="536"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:IHB_Ambulance.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>IHB Ambulance
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Bahrain has a <a href="/wiki/Universal_health_care" title="Universal health care">universal health care</a> system, dating back to 1960.<sup id="cite_ref-299" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-299">[299]</a></sup> Government-provided health care is free to Bahraini citizens and heavily subsidised for non-Bahrainis. Healthcare expenditure accounted for 4.5% of Bahrain's GDP, according to the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a>. Bahraini physicians and nurses form a majority of the country's workforce in the health sector, unlike neighbouring Gulf states.<sup id="cite_ref-300" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-300">[300]</a></sup> The first <a href="/wiki/Hospital" title="Hospital">hospital</a> in Bahrain was the <a href="/wiki/American_Mission_Hospital" title="American Mission Hospital">American Mission Hospital</a>, which opened in 1893 as a dispensary.<sup id="cite_ref-301" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-301">[301]</a></sup> The first public hospital, and also <a href="/wiki/Tertiary_referral_hospital" title="Tertiary referral hospital">tertiary hospital</a>, to open in Bahrain was the <a href="/wiki/Salmaniya_Medical_Complex" title="Salmaniya Medical Complex">Salmaniya Medical Complex</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Salmaniya" title="Salmaniya">Salmaniya</a> district of Manama, in 1957.<sup id="cite_ref-302" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-302">[302]</a></sup> Private hospitals are also present throughout the country, such as the <a href="/wiki/International_Hospital_of_Bahrain" title="International Hospital of Bahrain">International Hospital of Bahrain</a>. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">life expectancy</a> in Bahrain is 73 for males and 76 for females. Compared to many countries in the region, the prevalence of <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS" title="HIV/AIDS">AIDS</a> and <a href="/wiki/HIV" title="HIV">HIV</a> is relatively low.<sup id="cite_ref-UNDP_303-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNDP-303">[303]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">Malaria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">tuberculosis</a> (TB) do not constitute major problems in Bahrain as neither disease is indigenous to the country. As a result, cases of malaria and TB have declined in recent decades with cases of contractions amongst Bahraini nationals becoming rare.<sup id="cite_ref-UNDP_303-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNDP-303">[303]</a></sup> The Ministry of Health sponsors regular vaccination campaigns against TB and other diseases such as <a href="/wiki/Hepatitis_B" title="Hepatitis B">hepatitis B</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-UNDP_303-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNDP-303">[303]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-304" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-304">[304]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Bahrain is currently suffering from an <a href="/wiki/Obesity" title="Obesity">obesity</a> epidemic as 28.9% of all males and 38.2% of all females are classified as obese.<sup id="cite_ref-305" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-305">[305]</a></sup> Bahrain also has one of the highest prevalence of <a href="/wiki/Diabetes_mellitus" class="mw-redirect" title="Diabetes mellitus">diabetes</a> in the world (5th place), with more than 15% of the Bahraini population suffering from the disease, and accounting for 5% of deaths in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-306" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-306">[306]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cardiovascular_disease" title="Cardiovascular disease">Cardiovascular diseases</a> account for 32% of all deaths in Bahrain, being the number one cause of death in the country (the second being <a href="/wiki/Cancer" title="Cancer">cancer</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-307" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-307">[307]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sickle-cell_disease" class="mw-redirect" title="Sickle-cell disease">Sickle-cell anaemia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thalassaemia" class="mw-redirect" title="Thalassaemia">thalassaemia</a> are prevalent in the country, with a study concluding that 18% of Bahrainis are carriers of sickle-cell anaemia while 24% are carriers of thalassaemia.<sup id="cite_ref-308" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-308">[308]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bahrain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Bahrain" title="Culture of Bahrain">Culture of Bahrain</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Muharram_procession_2,_Manama,_Bahrain_(Feb_2005).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Muharram_procession_2%2C_Manama%2C_Bahrain_%28Feb_2005%29.jpg/220px-Muharram_procession_2%2C_Manama%2C_Bahrain_%28Feb_2005%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Muharram_procession_2%2C_Manama%2C_Bahrain_%28Feb_2005%29.jpg/330px-Muharram_procession_2%2C_Manama%2C_Bahrain_%28Feb_2005%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Muharram_procession_2%2C_Manama%2C_Bahrain_%28Feb_2005%29.jpg/440px-Muharram_procession_2%2C_Manama%2C_Bahrain_%28Feb_2005%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="773"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Muharram_procession_2,_Manama,_Bahrain_(Feb_2005).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Muharram_in_Bahrain" title="Muharram in Bahrain">Shia Muslims in Bahrain</a> strike their chests during <i><a href="/wiki/Mourning_of_Muharram" title="Mourning of Muharram">Muharram</a></i> in remembrance of <a href="/wiki/Imam_Hussain" class="mw-redirect" title="Imam Hussain">Imam Hussain</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Islam is the main religion, and Bahrainis are known for their tolerance towards the practice of other faiths.<sup id="cite_ref-309" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-309">[309]</a></sup> Intermarriages between Bahrainis and expatriates are not uncommon—there are many Filipino-Bahrainis like Filipino child actress <a href="/wiki/Mona_Louise_Rey" title="Mona Louise Rey">Mona Marbella Al-Alawi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-310" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-310">[310]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Rules regarding female attire are generally relaxed compared to regional neighbours; the traditional attire of women usually include the <a href="/wiki/Hijab" title="Hijab">hijab</a> or the <a href="/wiki/Abaya" title="Abaya">abaya</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Britannica_133-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-133">[133]</a></sup> Although the traditional male attire is the <a href="/wiki/Thawb" title="Thawb">thobe</a> which also includes traditional headdresses such as the <a href="/wiki/Keffiyeh" title="Keffiyeh">keffiyeh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Keffiyeh" title="Keffiyeh">ghutra</a> and <a href="/wiki/Agal_(accessory)" title="Agal (accessory)">agal</a>, Western clothing is common in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-Britannica_133-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-133">[133]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Although Bahrain legalized <a href="/wiki/Homosexuality" title="Homosexuality">homosexuality</a> in 1976, many homosexuals have since been arrested.<sup id="cite_ref-311" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-311">[311]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-312" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-312">[312]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-313" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-313">[313]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Art">Art</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bahrain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Art">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bahraini_art" title="Bahraini art">Bahraini art</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bahrain_wind_tower.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Bahrain_wind_tower.jpg/220px-Bahrain_wind_tower.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="330" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Bahrain_wind_tower.jpg/330px-Bahrain_wind_tower.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Bahrain_wind_tower.jpg/440px-Bahrain_wind_tower.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2730" data-file-height="4095"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bahrain_wind_tower.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A <a href="/wiki/Windcatcher" title="Windcatcher">wind tower</a> in Bahrain.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The modern art movement in the country officially emerged in the 1950s, culminating in the establishment of an art society. <a href="/wiki/Expressionism" title="Expressionism">Expressionism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Surrealism" title="Surrealism">surrealism</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Calligraphy" title="Calligraphy">calligraphic art</a> are the popular forms of art in the country. <a href="/wiki/Abstract_expressionism" title="Abstract expressionism">Abstract expressionism</a> has gained popularity in recent decades.<sup id="cite_ref-TGE_314-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TGE-314">[314]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pottery" title="Pottery">Pottery</a>-making and <a href="/wiki/Textile" title="Textile">textile</a>-weaving are also popular products that were widely made in Bahraini villages.<sup id="cite_ref-TGE_314-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TGE-314">[314]</a></sup> Arabic calligraphy grew in popularity as the <a href="/wiki/Bahraini_government" class="mw-redirect" title="Bahraini government">Bahraini government</a> was an active patron in <a href="/wiki/Islamic_art" title="Islamic art">Islamic art</a>, culminating in the establishment of an Islamic museum, <a href="/wiki/Beit_Al_Quran" title="Beit Al Quran">Beit Al Quran</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-TGE_314-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TGE-314">[314]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Bahrain_National_Museum" title="Bahrain National Museum">Bahrain national museum</a> houses a permanent <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_art" title="Contemporary art">contemporary art</a> exhibition.<sup id="cite_ref-315" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-315">[315]</a></sup> The annual Spring of Culture <sup id="cite_ref-316" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-316">[316]</a></sup> festival run by the Bahrain Authority for Culture and Antiquities<sup id="cite_ref-317" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-317">[317]</a></sup> has become a popular event promoting performance arts in the Kingdom. The <a href="/wiki/Architecture" title="Architecture">architecture</a> of Bahrain is similar to that of its neighbours in the Persian Gulf. The <a href="/wiki/Windcatcher" title="Windcatcher">wind tower</a>, which generates natural ventilation in a house, is a common sight on old buildings, particularly in the old districts of Manama and <a href="/wiki/Muharraq" title="Muharraq">Muharraq</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ali_318-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ali-318">[318]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bahrain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Literature_of_Bahrain" class="mw-redirect" title="Literature of Bahrain">Literature of Bahrain</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Literature retains a strong tradition in the country; most traditional writers and poets write in the <a href="/wiki/Classical_Arabic" title="Classical Arabic">classical Arabic</a> style. In recent years, the number of younger poets influenced by <a href="/wiki/Western_literature" title="Western literature">western literature</a> are rising, most writing in <a href="/wiki/Free_verse" title="Free verse">free verse</a> and often including political or personal content.<sup id="cite_ref-EC_319-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EC-319">[319]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ali_Al_Shargawi" title="Ali Al Shargawi">Ali Al Shargawi</a>, a decorated longtime poet, was described in 2011 by <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Al_Shorfa&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Al Shorfa (page does not exist)">Al Shorfa</a></i> as the literary icon of Bahrain.<sup id="cite_ref-AS_320-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AS-320">[320]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In literature, Bahrain was the site of the ancient land of <a href="/wiki/Dilmun" title="Dilmun">Dilmun</a> mentioned in the <a href="/wiki/Epic_of_Gilgamesh" title="Epic of Gilgamesh">Epic of Gilgamesh</a>. Legend also states that it was the location of the <a href="/wiki/Garden_of_Eden" title="Garden of Eden">Garden of Eden</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT_321-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-321">[321]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-LAT_322-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LAT-322">[322]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bahrain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Bahrain" title="Music of Bahrain">Music of Bahrain</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The music style in Bahrain is similar to that of its neighbors. The <a href="/wiki/Khaliji_(music)" title="Khaliji (music)">Khaliji</a> style of music, which is <a href="/wiki/Folk_music" title="Folk music">folk music</a>, is popular in the country. The <a href="/wiki/Sawt_(music)" title="Sawt (music)">sawt</a> style of music, which involves a complex form of urban music, performed by an <a href="/wiki/Oud" title="Oud">Oud</a> (plucked lute), a <a href="/wiki/Violin" title="Violin">violin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mirwas" title="Mirwas">mirwas</a> (a drum), is also popular in Bahrain.<sup id="cite_ref-AUC_323-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AUC-323">[323]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ali_Bahar" title="Ali Bahar">Ali Bahar</a> was one of the most famous singers in Bahrain. He performed his music with his Band <i>Al-Ekhwa</i> (<i>The Brothers</i>). Bahrain was also the site of the first <a href="/wiki/Recording_studio" title="Recording studio">recording studio</a> amongst the Persian Gulf states.<sup id="cite_ref-AUC_323-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AUC-323">[323]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Entertainment">Entertainment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bahrain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Entertainment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Category:Entertainment_in_Bahrain" title="Category:Entertainment in Bahrain">Category:Entertainment in Bahrain</a>
      </div> 
      <p>With regards to cultural and tourism activities, the Ministry of Culture<sup id="cite_ref-324" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-324">[324]</a></sup> organizes a number of annual festivals. such as the Spring of Culture in March and April, the Bahrain Summer Festival and Ta’a Al-Shabab from August to September, and the Bahrain International Music Festival in October which features musical and theatrical performances, lectures, and much more. </p>
      <p>As for cultural sites, residents, visitors, and tourists can re-live history through Bahrain’s many historical sites. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bahrain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Bahrain" title="Sport in Bahrain">Sport in Bahrain</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Bahrain is the first nation other than <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States of America</a> to host <a href="/wiki/International_Mixed_Martial_Arts_Federation" title="International Mixed Martial Arts Federation">International Mixed Martial Arts Federation</a> World Championships of Amateur MMA.<sup id="cite_ref-325" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-325">[325]</a></sup> Bahrain have recorded an influx in global athletes visiting the nation for Mixed Martial Arts training during 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-326" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-326">[326]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2018, Cricket was introduced in Bahrain under initiative of KHK Sports and Exelon.<sup id="cite_ref-327" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-327">[327]</a></sup> Bahrain Premier League 2018 comprised six franchise squads of 13 resident cricketers competing in the T20 format. The teams were SRam MRam Falcons, Kalaam Knight-Riders, Intex Lions, Bahrain Super Giants, Four Square Challengers and Awan Warriors.<sup id="cite_ref-328" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-328">[328]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Association football</a> is the most popular sport in Bahrain.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated6_329-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated6-329">[329]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bahrain_national_football_team" title="Bahrain national football team">Bahrain's national football team</a> has competed multiple times at the <a href="/wiki/AFC_Asian_Cup" title="AFC Asian Cup">Asian Cup</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arab_Nations_Cup" title="Arab Nations Cup">Arab Nations Cup</a> and played in the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cup</a> qualifiers, though it has never qualified for the World Cup.<sup id="cite_ref-330" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-330">[330]</a></sup> Bahrain has its own <a href="/wiki/Ranking" title="Ranking">top-tier</a> domestic professional <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_association_football" title="Geography of association football">football league</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Bahraini_Premier_League" title="Bahraini Premier League">Bahraini Premier League</a>. <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Bahrain#Basketball" title="Sport in Bahrain">Basketball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Bahrain#Rugby" title="Sport in Bahrain">rugby</a> and <a href="/wiki/Horse_racing" title="Horse racing">horse racing</a> are also widely popular in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated6_329-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated6-329">[329]</a></sup> The government of Bahrain also sponsors a <a href="/wiki/UCI_WorldTeam" title="UCI WorldTeam">UCI WorldTeam</a> cycling team, <a href="/wiki/Bahrain%E2%80%93Merida_Pro_Cycling_Team" class="mw-redirect" title="Bahrain–Merida Pro Cycling Team">Bahrain–Merida</a>, which participated in the <a href="/wiki/2017_Tour_de_France" title="2017 Tour de France">2017 Tour de France</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-331" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-331">[331]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-332" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-332">[332]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Brave_Combat_Federation" title="Brave Combat Federation">Brave Combat Federation</a> is a Bahrain-based Mixed Martial Arts promotion which has hosted events in Bahrain, United Arab Emirates, Brazil, Kazakhstan, and India. Bahrain MMA Federation (BMMAF) has been set up under the patronage of Sheikh <a href="/wiki/Khalid_bin_Hamad_Al_Khalifa" title="Khalid bin Hamad Al Khalifa">Khalid bin Hamad Al Khalifa</a> and the jurisdiction of the Sports Minister, Sheikh <a href="/wiki/Nasser_bin_Hamad_Al_Khalifa" title="Nasser bin Hamad Al Khalifa">Nasser bin Hamad Al Khalifa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-333" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-333">[333]</a></sup> The development of MMA in the nation is convened through KHK MMA, which owns <a href="/wiki/Brave_Combat_Federation" title="Brave Combat Federation">Brave Combat Federation</a> which is the largest Mixed Martial Arts promotion in the Middle East.<sup id="cite_ref-334" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-334">[334]</a></sup> Bahrain will be hosting Amateur World Championships 2017 in association with <a href="/wiki/International_Mixed_Martial_Arts_Federation" title="International Mixed Martial Arts Federation">International Mixed Martial Arts Federation</a>. Bahrain will be the first Asian and Arab country to host the amateur MMA championship.<sup id="cite_ref-335" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-335">[335]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:2007_Bahrain_GP_podium.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/2007_Bahrain_GP_podium.jpg/220px-2007_Bahrain_GP_podium.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/2007_Bahrain_GP_podium.jpg/330px-2007_Bahrain_GP_podium.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/2007_Bahrain_GP_podium.jpg/440px-2007_Bahrain_GP_podium.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="600"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:2007_Bahrain_GP_podium.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The podium ceremony at the <a href="/wiki/2007_Bahrain_Grand_Prix" title="2007 Bahrain Grand Prix">2007 Bahrain Grand Prix</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Bahrain has a <a href="/wiki/Bahrain_International_Circuit" title="Bahrain International Circuit">Formula One race-track</a>, which hosted the inaugural <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Air" title="Gulf Air">Gulf Air</a> <a href="/wiki/Bahrain_Grand_Prix" title="Bahrain Grand Prix">Bahrain Grand Prix</a> on 4 April 2004, the first in an Arab country. This was followed by the Bahrain Grand Prix in 2005. Bahrain hosted the opening Grand Prix of the 2006 season on 12 March of that year. Both the above races were won by <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Alonso" title="Fernando Alonso">Fernando Alonso</a> of <a href="/wiki/Renault" title="Renault">Renault</a>. The race has since been hosted annually, except for <a href="/wiki/2011_Bahrain_Grand_Prix" title="2011 Bahrain Grand Prix">2011</a> when it was cancelled due to <a href="/wiki/Bahraini_uprising_of_2011" title="Bahraini uprising of 2011">ongoing anti-government protests</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-autosport89525_336-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autosport89525-336">[336]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/2012_Bahrain_Grand_Prix" title="2012 Bahrain Grand Prix">2012</a> race occurred despite concerns of the safety of the teams and the ongoing <a href="/wiki/2012_Bahrain_Grand_Prix_protests" title="2012 Bahrain Grand Prix protests">protests</a> in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-337" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-337">[337]</a></sup> The decision to hold the race despite ongoing protests and violence<sup id="cite_ref-race_on_338-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-race_on-338">[338]</a></sup> has been described as "controversial" by <a href="/wiki/Al_Jazeera_English" title="Al Jazeera English">Al Jazeera English</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-339" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-339">[339]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/CNN" title="CNN">CNN</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-340" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-340">[340]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Agence_France-Presse" title="Agence France-Presse">AFP</a><sup id="cite_ref-341" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-341">[341]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Sky_News" title="Sky News">Sky News</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-342" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-342">[342]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Independent" title="The Independent">The Independent</a></i> named it "one of the most controversial in the history of the sport".<sup id="cite_ref-343" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-343">[343]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2006, Bahrain also hosted its inaugural Australian <a href="/wiki/Supercars_Championship" title="Supercars Championship">V8 Supercar</a> event dubbed the "<i>Desert 400</i>". The V8s returned every November to the <a href="/wiki/Sakhir" title="Sakhir">Sakhir</a> circuit until 2010, in which it was the second event of the series. The series has not returned since. The <a href="/wiki/Bahrain_International_Circuit" title="Bahrain International Circuit">Bahrain International Circuit</a> also features a full-length <a href="/wiki/Dragstrip" title="Dragstrip">dragstrip</a> where the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bahrain_Drag_Racing_Club&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Bahrain Drag Racing Club (page does not exist)">Bahrain Drag Racing Club</a> has organised invitational events featuring some of Europe's top drag racing teams to try to raise the profile of the sport in the Middle East.<sup id="cite_ref-344" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-344">[344]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On August 3, 2020, the Kingdom of Bahrain bought a minority stake in the <a href="/wiki/Paris_FC" title="Paris FC">Paris F.C.</a>, a team that plays in France’s second tier. Bahrain’s entry into the soccer club came with people criticizing that the country is trying to whitewash its <a href="/wiki/Human_rights" title="Human rights">human rights</a> record and this is another way of buying influence in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-345" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-345">[345]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Holidays">Holidays</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Bahrain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Holidays">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>On 1 September 2006, Bahrain changed its weekend from being Thursdays and Fridays to Fridays and Saturdays, in order to have a day of the weekend shared with the rest of the world. Notable holidays in the country are listed below: </p> 
      <table class="wikitable sortable"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th>Date</th> 
         <th>English name</th> 
         <th>Local (<a href="/wiki/Arabic_Language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic Language">Arabic</a>) name</th> 
         <th>Description </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>1 January</td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/New_Year%27s_Day" title="New Year's Day">New Year's Day</a></td> 
         <td>رأس السنة الميلادية</td> 
         <td>The <a href="/wiki/Gregorian_calendar" title="Gregorian calendar">Gregorian</a> New Year's Day. </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>1 May</td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Labour_Day" title="Labour Day">Labour Day</a></td> 
         <td>يوم العمال</td> 
         <td>Locally called "Eid Al Oumal" (Workers' Day). </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>16 December</td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/National_Day" class="mw-redirect" title="National Day">National Day</a></td> 
         <td>اليوم الوطني</td> 
         <td>National Day of Bahrain.<sup id="cite_ref-346" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-346">[346]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>17 December</td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Accession_Day" class="mw-redirect" title="Accession Day">Accession Day</a></td> 
         <td>يوم الجلوس</td> 
         <td>Accession Day for the late Amir <i>Sh. Isa Bin Salman Al Khalifa</i> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>1st <i><a href="/wiki/Muharram" title="Muharram">Muharram</a></i></td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Islamic_New_Year" title="Islamic New Year">Islamic New Year</a></td> 
         <td>رأس السنة الهجرية</td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Islamic_Calendar" class="mw-redirect" title="Islamic Calendar">Islamic</a> New Year (also known as: <i>Hijri New Year</i>). </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>9th, 10th <i>Muharram</i></td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Day_of_Ashura" class="mw-redirect" title="Day of Ashura">Day of <i>Ashura</i></a></td> 
         <td>عاشوراء</td> 
         <td>Represented on the 9th and 10th day of the Hijri month of Muharram. Coincided with the memory of the martyrdom of <a href="/wiki/Imam_Hussein" class="mw-redirect" title="Imam Hussein">Imam Hussein</a>. </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>12th <i><a href="/wiki/Rabi%27_al-awwal" class="mw-redirect" title="Rabi' al-awwal">Rabiul Awwal</a></i></td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Mawlid" title="Mawlid">Prophet Muhammad's birthday</a></td> 
         <td>المولد النبوي</td> 
         <td>Commemorates <a href="/wiki/Prophet" title="Prophet">Prophet</a> <a href="/wiki/Muhammad" title="Muhammad">Muhammad</a>'s birthday, celebrated in most parts of the Muslim world. </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>1st, 2nd, and 3rd <i><a href="/wiki/Shawwal" title="Shawwal">Shawwal</a></i></td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Eid_ul-Fitr" class="mw-redirect" title="Eid ul-Fitr">Little Feast</a></td> 
         <td>عيد الفطر</td> 
         <td>Commemorates the end of <a href="/wiki/Ramadan" title="Ramadan">Ramadan</a>. </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>9th <i><a href="/wiki/Dhu_al-Hijjah" title="Dhu al-Hijjah">Zulhijjah</a></i></td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Day_of_Arafat" class="mw-redirect" title="Day of Arafat">Arafat Day</a></td> 
         <td>يوم عرفة</td> 
         <td>Commemoration of Muhammad's final sermon and completion of the message of Islam. </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>10th, 11th, 12th, and 13th <i><a href="/wiki/Dhu_al-Hijjah" title="Dhu al-Hijjah">Zulhijjah</a></i></td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Eid_ul-Adha" class="mw-redirect" title="Eid ul-Adha">Feast of the Sacrifice</a></td> 
         <td>عيد الأضحى</td> 
         <td>Commemorates <a href="/wiki/Abraham" title="Abraham">Ibrahim</a>'s willingness to sacrifice his son. Also known as the <i>Big Feast</i> (celebrated from the 10th to 13th). </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table>

           <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite id="CITEREFHoles2001" class="citation book cs1">Holes, Clive (2001). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=bJLjAKH7-rIC&amp;pg=PR24"><i>Dialect, Culture, and Society in Eastern Arabia: Glossary</i></a>. <i>Clive Holes</i>. pp.&nbsp;XXIV–XXVI. <a href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a>&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9004107630" title="Special:BookSources/9004107630"><bdi>9004107630</bdi></a>. <q>Thus the pre-Islamic ethno-linguistic situation in eastern Arabia appear to have been a mixed tribal population of partially Christianised Arabs of diverse origins who probably spoke different old Arabian vernaculars; a mobile Persian-speaking population, possibly of traders and administrators, with strong links to Persia, with which they maintained close contact; a sedentary, non-tribal community of Aramaic-speaking farmers; a Persian clergy, which we know for certain, used Syriac as a language of liturgy and general writing, probably alongside Persian as a spoken language.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dialect%2C+Culture%2C+and+Society+in+Eastern+Arabia%3A+Glossary&amp;rft.pages=XXIV-XXVI&amp;rft.date=2001&amp;rft.isbn=9004107630&amp;rft.aulast=Holes&amp;rft.aufirst=Clive&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DbJLjAKH7-rIC%26pg%3DPR24&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ABahrain" class="Z3988"></span></span> </li>
